        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer392757480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4782896138954294662"><b>* I just lowered my rating from four stars to a generous three because, having read the second book, how I feel about this book as a whole and its ending is <i>much</i> more negative than before.</b><br/><br/>See, I have this really annoying problem (yes, it's a problem. Others may call it a skill, but trust me, when you have it, it's a <i>problem</i>) where, if I go into something knowing that there's a huge twist in the end, I will introspect every little detail that I normally would have overlooked had I not known there</span>
  <span id="freeText4782896138954294662" style="display:none"><b>* I just lowered my rating from four stars to a generous three because, having read the second book, how I feel about this book as a whole and its ending is <i>much</i> more negative than before.</b><br /><br />See, I have this really annoying problem (yes, it's a problem. Others may call it a skill, but trust me, when you have it, it's a <i>problem</i>) where, if I go into something knowing that there's a huge twist in the end, I will introspect every little detail that I normally would have overlooked had I not known there was a twist, leading to me pinning down the twist long before it is revealed, which also leads to my enjoyment in the mystery being lowered significantly. The huge twist in the movie <i>Identity</i>, which seemingly <i>everybody</i> was blind-sighted by? Guessed it in the first two minutes of the movie. Pretty much every single adult murder mystery, which inevitably ends in a twist ending? Pssh, easy; the baby's the rapist. <br /><br /><i>The Madman's Daughter</i>, however, is quite the enigma. I'd gone into <i>The Madman's Daughter</i> knowing that there'd be a twist ending (and for those who have the same problem I have, I'm sorry, but you were bound to find out there's a twist eventually), and while I, in the end, got most of the twist pinned down, how I got to that twist was different than I get to most others. The case with most twist endings is that I come up with at most two theories, and at least one of them slightly resembles the twist at the end. But in the case of <i>The Madman's Daughter</i>, I went through <i>multiple</i> theories as to what the twist was, what the monster was, and the solution to most of the novel's mysteries. And then, when I discarded one theory and thought I'd never see it again, I only ended up bringing it back into play mere percentages later.<br /><br />And even though I did see the major twist coming (mind you, however, only about ten percentages before it was revealed, which is pretty damn impressive for the book), the fact that I saw the twist coming didn't impact my enjoyment in the novel in the slightest, unlike most cases. Sheperd incorporated each and every twist into <i>The Madman's Daughter</i> with such finesse and cleverness that each twist was enchanting, and I was able to look over the fact that I had saw them coming and just turn the pages in awe as I had come to realization of how Sherperd had woven the twists into the story. <br /><br />And speaking of the story, what a story it was! <i>The Madman's Daughter</i> opens with a bang, and ends with an even <i>bigger</i> bang, full of complete and utter brilliance at every corner. The middle, however, is where I feel the novel met its faults. While much of the middle section of <i>The Madman's Daughter</i> is filled with suspense, intrigue, and secrets, much of it is also filled with relationship angst, something I am definitely not a fan of. And while I wasn't completely sold on either of the romances in <i>The Madman's Daughter</i>, which is probably why reading about Juliet go on about either of the boys was a bore to me, I definitely appreciate and almost admire how Sherperd made the love triangle play out. <br /><br />Juliet was an absolutely amazing character, and I found myself loving her very soon in the novel. She's smart, sassy, strong, and while she is a bit sidetracked by the boys at times, I found her to be an amazing heroine and protagonist to follow around, and her sparkling wit and how she dealt with the misogyny of her father was amazing. The character of Juliet's father, Doctor Henri Moreau, was also one that was well developed, and he was a character I found myself loving to hate. The two love interests of Juliet, however, like I had mentioned earlier, never really sparked much of a reaction from me, and my opinion on both of them are pretty lukewarm, but they, too, are met with a good deal of character development throughout the novel. <br /><br />Chocked full of suspense, interesting and clever plot twists, creepy-crawlies, great side-characters, and truly disturbing and horrifying moments, <i>The Madman's Daughter</i> will surely appeal to any horror fans looking for a chilling read. I'm not entirely sure where the story could go from the ending of <i>The Madman's Daughter</i> forward, but either way, I thoroughly look forward to reading the next book in this trilogy and seeing what else Megan Sheperd has in store. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4782896138954294662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11506060773145623331">My rating: 2.5 of 5 stars<br/>A copy of The Madman's Daughter was provided to me by Balzer + Bray/Edelweiss for review purposes.<br/><br/>'Dead flesh and sharpened scalpels didn't bother me. I was my father's daughter, after all. My nightmares were made of darker things.'<br/><br/>I feel the need to start off by saying I didn't dislike this book but obviously considering my rating I have some explaining to do. There was creepiness, there was a decent story line, but the pacing was so incredibly slow that it had an adver</span>
  <span id="freeText11506060773145623331" style="display:none">My rating: 2.5 of 5 stars<br>A copy of The Madman's Daughter was provided to me by Balzer + Bray/Edelweiss for review purposes.<br><br>'Dead flesh and sharpened scalpels didn't bother me. I was my father's daughter, after all. My nightmares were made of darker things.'<br><br>I feel the need to start off by saying I didn't dislike this book but obviously considering my rating I have some explaining to do. There was creepiness, there was a decent story line, but the pacing was so incredibly slow that it had an adverse effect on my overall opinion on this gothic retelling.<br><br>Let me tell you guys, the beginning of this story had so much creepy going on it was amazing. I remember starting this book, finishing the first couple of chapters, stopping for a second and saying to myself, "This is going to be so awesome." Juliet seemed to be a very promising main character and I couldn't wait to hear her story. But the gothic thriller aspect seemed to be put on the back burner and definitely became less of a focus. What did it end up focusing on? Romance, of course.<br><br>There was so much emphasis put on the romance and her being torn between two men, her swooning and constant need to fan herself that I would go so far as to consider this 'historical-romance-lite'. If not for the creepy and exceptionally gruesome bits in this story I don't believe I would have finished this. As it was though, the romance didn't feel fitting in this type of story, like an irregular puzzle piece.<br><br>I had been forewarned that the middle dawdled but that the ending was a big shocker so that gave me hope. The pacing was definitely off for the vast majority of the middle portion and didn't actually start picking up until almost the very end of the book. The big reveal happened and it was definitely the most interesting aspect of the entire story but it happened a little too late for me. There wasn't a slow build-up to the grand finale which would have made this immensely better. Instead we received a storyline that plodded along, lacking in intensity, never quite gaining enough steam, and then we're hit with the big ending. The middle section certainly required something more for me to still be invested enough in the story to be excited for when the big conclusion finally did happen. <br><br>Oh, and there's a cliffhanger. Naturally. I think my response to that final page was something along the lines of, "Dude. For real?" Considering I was more than a bit bored through the majority of this story I was at least hoping we'd get some answers. I had still considered giving #2 a shot since sometimes it takes the first book to build the story (in a series) and book 2 is where we can finally get to the meat of the story. But my understanding was that this was a retelling of the Island of Dr. Moreau, however, the summary for book 2 states it was written: with inspiration from Robert Louis Stevenson's 'THE STRANGE CASE OF DR JEKYLL AND MR HYDE' and I'm not sure I feel about the mixing of multiple retellings.<br><br><div>
  <a href="http://sweet-tidbits.blogspot.com/" title="Sweet Tidbits" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

  </a>

<div id="review_736264753" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/736264753?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=r2r-complete">r2r-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-with-abbie">read-with-abbie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>,

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer736264753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12441519418303935092"><b>
  <i>“The world knew my father as a villain. I knew him as the thin man in a tweed suit who carried me on his shoulders during the Royal Guard’s parades. I needed to know which man my father was – the monster, or the misunderstood genius.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421061985i/13317055._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was a really creepy and entertaining story, with several twists to the tale!<br/><br/><br/>I really liked Juliet and the other characters in this book. I felt sorry for Juliet and everything she had been through with her father being labelled as a madman, and her mother d</span>
  <span id="freeText12441519418303935092" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“The world knew my father as a villain. I knew him as the thin man in a tweed suit who carried me on his shoulders during the Royal Guard’s parades. I needed to know which man my father was – the monster, or the misunderstood genius.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421061985i/13317055._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was a really creepy and entertaining story, with several twists to the tale!<br><br><br>I really liked Juliet and the other characters in this book. I felt sorry for Juliet and everything she had been through with her father being labelled as a madman, and her mother dying and leaving her an orphan. The poor girl really was all alone in the world, and with no money, and no-one to help her, I could understand why she would want to go to a strange island to possibly be reunited with her long-thought-dead father.<br><br><b>
  <i>“I should have told Lucy she couldn’t visit. Where I was going, she couldn’t come. It was a bit further than Bedford.<br>Montgomery opened the door, clearly surprised. “Miss Moreau. What are you doing here?”<br>The carpetbag fell at his feet. My heart was racing.<br>“I’m coming with you,” I said.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421061882i/13317044.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The storyline in this was pretty good, and I liked that it was creepy in places! The not-knowing what experiments Juliet’s father was really doing, the screaming of the animals from his operating room at night, the way he so calmly tried to drown someone, and the question over just how wicked he really was all added to the tension, and then the twists really started piling up!<br><br><b>
  <i>“Father folded his hands. “I am in pursuit of the ideal living form. Just like all of us, wouldn’t you say? The same reason we choose mates and procreate. We want to create something better than ourselves. Perfection. To me, perfection is a being with the reason of man but the natural innocence of children – or animals. I have come so close to achieving it. You have no idea how close.””</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421061882i/13317043.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There was some romance, and it did turn into a love triangle, with the question being whether Juliet would choose the dashing Edward Prince, or the servant boy, turned mad-doctor’s assistant Montgomery, and it really wasn’t clear which one she would pick until almost the end of the book!<br><br><br><b>
  <i>“Juliet, don’t tell me you didn’t know. Montgomery’s been in love with you since the day you found him again. Long before that, come to think of it. He’s been in love with the mere idea of you for years.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421062821i/13317153.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>
  <i>“We’ll go back to London and none of it will matter. It’ll just be you and me Juliet…”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421062971i/13317256._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending to this wasn’t perfect, and I have to say that I’m really intrigued to see what happens in the next book in the series. This wasn’t a total cliff-hanger, but it wasn’t the ending that I was expecting either, and I really want to know how things work out!<br><br><b>
  <i>““We belong together. Not to serve your father’s mad experiment. But because we’re the same.” His open palm covered my heart, just grazing the exposed skin above my collar. I gasped at his touch. Fear and thrill were divided by such a fine line that I couldn’t tell which plucked at the tight strings in my chest. And was he really so wrong? I did know about the darkness he spoke of.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421062821i/13317155._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>8 out of 10<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12441519418303935092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_351340529" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351340529" />
    <a title="Joy (joyous reads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4352734-joy-joyous-reads"><img alt="Joy (joyous reads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526951297p2/4352734.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joy (joyous reads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joy (joyous reads)" href="/user/show/4352734-joy-joyous-reads">Joy (joyous reads)</a>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351340529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10626596786908878411"><b>head desk</b><br/> <br/>this is all but the reaction you will get<br/>from this reader who’d rather soon forget<br/>this novel’s hype ran at a fever pitch<br/>but it gave me hives and made me itch.<br/> <br/>it could’ve been so good<br/>and I’d imagine most of you loved it<br/>as you should<br/>but I really could not digest<br/>a love triangle is not what I behest<br/> <br/>i’m sorry I could no longer continue<br/>i’m sorry my enthusiasm you couldn’t renew<br/>a heroine whose heart was not in it<br/>but for two boys – I just don’t get it.<br/> <br/>i’m sure there’s more to this story<br/>but </span>
  <span id="freeText10626596786908878411" style="display:none"><b>head desk</b><br /> <br />this is all but the reaction you will get<br />from this reader who’d rather soon forget<br />this novel’s hype ran at a fever pitch<br />but it gave me hives and made me itch.<br /> <br />it could’ve been so good<br />and I’d imagine most of you loved it<br />as you should<br />but I really could not digest<br />a love triangle is not what I behest<br /> <br />i’m sorry I could no longer continue<br />i’m sorry my enthusiasm you couldn’t renew<br />a heroine whose heart was not in it<br />but for two boys – I just don’t get it.<br /> <br />i’m sure there’s more to this story<br />but I’ve already invested my time – surely!<br />i have thousands of books on my shelves<br />clamouring like little elves<br />wanting and crying for my attention<br />for which I’d rather give my devotion!<br /> <br />i’m sure you’ll argue that I’m missing out<br />i’m sure I’m missing half of what it’s about<br />but I’ve already spent a couple of curses<br />colourful words and colourful verses<br />in fact, I’ve ranted and raged in my bedroom<br />as my husband looked at me like I’m a loon.<br />this is the kind of reaction I get<br />with that geometrical shape, you bet.<br /> <br />i’m afraid, my dear, this is where we part<br />i know writing is an art<br />the author spent sweat and tears<br />so please read it anyway<br />and ignore my jeers.<br /><br />I'm sure my feelings expressed were clear. I just couldn't stand love triangles and the heroine's reactions didn't make any sense to me. I couldn't, for the life of me, figure out why she's more focused on the two boys when there were so many other things going on right in front of her. The book's blurb states that it's a "breathless gothic", and it was for the most part of what I've managed to read, but damn. It's the romance that I could've gone without. <br /><br />I mentioned this on one of my reading statuses that instead of her focusing on the fact that her father didn't care enough to send for her when she was as poor as a church mice and on the verge of prostituting herself, she was more concerned about her confusing feelings toward Edward and Montgomery. I hated that she'd become <b>that girl</b> when she could've been a stronger, smarter woman. <br /><br />And I know I'm missing out. I've not even gone deep into the story of the island. I didn't get to find out who Edward was or where he really came from. And I wanted to know why the humans there are deformed. But I just couldn't get over this huge wall of a stupid love triangle. I just couldn't give a fcuk. I hated reading Juliet's incessant thoughts about how the two boys set her on fire. <br /><br />Right then. I think I should go read the original work. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_479893682" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/479893682" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413275441p2/10890208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/479893682?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=could-have-been-so-much-better">could-have-been-so-much-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=omg-the-cover-people">omg-the-cover-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=me-likes-you">me-likes-you</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer479893682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12087082823320180124">See more reviews at <a href='http://yamidnightreads.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Midnight Reads</a><br/><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Add some science, romance, grotesque, deformed animals and an abandoned Victorian gothic setting in the historical era and there you have, The Madman's Daughter. This book cannot be described as fun, weaved heavily with mystery and horrific writing, this book should be more described as like the title suggests madness. Pure madness.<br/><br/>Ever since her mother died and her father, a once loved scientist was also pronounced to be dead, Juliet's life has been</span>
  <span id="freeText12087082823320180124" style="display:none">See more reviews at <a href="http://yamidnightreads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Midnight Reads</a><br /><br /><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />Add some science, romance, grotesque, deformed animals and an abandoned Victorian gothic setting in the historical era and there you have, The Madman's Daughter. This book cannot be described as fun, weaved heavily with mystery and horrific writing, this book should be more described as like the title suggests madness. Pure madness.<br /><br />Ever since her mother died and her father, a once loved scientist was also pronounced to be dead, Juliet's life has been nothing but eventful. As a maid, with no one to turn to, she tries not to think about the one thing that made her life turn upside down. Yet when one small clue of her father being still alive appears in front of her, she immediately takes up the chance--instead of finding her father, she is once again face to face with Montgomery, her father's assistant from when he was still in London. Soon enough, she discovers that her father is actually alive, hidden on a remote island far away from London. And with Montgomery by her side, they set sea on their journey. The more time she spends on the island, the more truths she discovers and the more she realises that she should have never come.<br /><br />Juliet Moreau, daughter of the madman scientist was the main character. She started off as a solid, capable character who wasn't the slightest bit lady-like. Yet as the story deepened, she began to lose her strong charisma and became marginally irritating and boring. This wasn't a huge issue but I couldn't help but feel my impressions towards Juliet slip lower and lower as the story grew to the end. However this is not to say that she didn't lose her spunk and skepsism, even towards her father. I loved her cautiousness and her thoughtful actions, while not too slow but not too impulsive--also, her layers of depth and secrets about her past are nothing less than compelling and fascinating.<br /><br />What really nullified my enjoyment of The Madman's Daughter was the romance. We have a muted angst going on with the addition of a love triangle (yeah... laaaame.) There is Montgomery, the gentleman that Juliet has known for most of her life and the castaway, Edward who was saved by Juliet and Montgomery when they were sailing along on the ship to the island where Juliet’s father had taken asylum to hide--which mind you, held a distinct, creepy atmosphere. Anywho, I was incredibly astonished to come across such a cliché romance in a promising, thriller-ly novel. Sure, a romance can be here, but it doesn't have to be so overpowered and stereotyped. It makes no sense, if Juliet has finally become independent, after dropping her position as a maid, it doesn't mean she needs to have two guys all insanely into her. For a novel I could have given 5 stars, it was lowered due to this main factor.<br /><br />Due to the ineffective romance plot, life on the island isn't quite as consistently eventful. There are details that I wished could have been used effort elsewhere, instead of some monotonous jungle walks. The plot came in a little too late--there isn't much of a distinct one, more like an ongoing background mystery--and by the time the plot had more focus, the book ended. Also on a cliff-hanger (!!) but luckily I'm starting the sequel sometime very soon. Another small niggle was the fact that this was a historian set novel. I actually felt that this genre label was wasted in this book. There are only a few pieces of dialogue that actually felt like it was said in the historical era, so it bugged me to remind myself that this was set in the more ancient times. It was seriously off-putting to read a piece of dialogue and have 'hitherto' inserted randomly--it did not go with any other elements.<br /><br />The Madman's Daughter was disappointing in the romance and plot-- therefore meaning the book became a little monotonous at times but I still appreciated Megan Shepherd's idea, writing and main character. I can't wait for Her Dark Curiosity!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12087082823320180124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1068264005" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1068264005" />
    <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction"><img alt="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605816027p2/2905339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1068264005?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction">Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780062246110" href="/book/show/16145429-the-madman-s-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1068264005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10078124714926111472">This is a young adult novel with a love triangle. You have been warned.<br/><blockquote>
<br/>“Edward and Montgomery were suddenly both by my side, each taking an arm.<br/><br/>My face burned as I looked between them. Two boys, two sets of hands on my wrists. One rough and calloused, the other strong yet smooth. My emotions knotted tighter, threatening to cut off my circulation.”</blockquote><br/><br/>I picked it up knowing this and expecting the above because I was seduced by the plot. The “madman” is actually Dr. Moreau. Yes, <i>that</i> Dr. Moreau. The </span>
  <span id="freeText10078124714926111472" style="display:none">This is a young adult novel with a love triangle. You have been warned.<br><blockquote>
<br>“Edward and Montgomery were suddenly both by my side, each taking an arm.<br><br>My face burned as I looked between them. Two boys, two sets of hands on my wrists. One rough and calloused, the other strong yet smooth. My emotions knotted tighter, threatening to cut off my circulation.”</blockquote><br><br>I picked it up knowing this and expecting the above because I was seduced by the plot. The “madman” is actually Dr. Moreau. Yes, <i>that</i> Dr. Moreau. The one who, in my dreams, creates these lovelies:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413397561i/11504820.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412791802i/11423943._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Dr. Moreau was basically run out of town and his reputation ruined after his nefarious experiments came to light. He abandoned both his wife and young daughter and high-tailed it to an island. Flash-forward a few years and Juliette is now a teenager eeking out a living as a maid. She stumbles across some evidence to the location of her long-lost father and, though she is haunted by memories of him, he is the only family she has left and she sets off an adventure to track him down. She may wish she had never found that first clue before it’s all said and done . . .<br><br>I really enjoyed most of this book. It has a very well done sense of place and maintained its creepy gothic “what the heck is going on” atmosphere throughout. The love triangle was unnecessary and I didn’t give a rats patootie about it but I’m too old to care about teen crushes and flip flopping between handsome boys. I wanted more gruesome surgery scenes but what is here was enough to make me happy. <br><br><blockquote>“To me, blood smelled like home.”</blockquote><br><br>I liked Juliette. She fears she is too much like her father; cold, a little blood-thirsty, perhaps, maybe even a little mad. She is very honest in her thoughts and I found this realistic as well as refreshing. She was the only character who really captured my attention. <br><br>There are many twists and turns and secrets to be revealed and I was surprised more than once at a few of the reveals but if I’m being honest it was way too long. Probably 80 or so pages too long. The backdrop, the horror (quite repulsive at times) and the evocative writing elevates this above most of what’s out there and the ending was perfect. If this interests you check it out. I don’t think you’ll be disappointed.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10078124714926111472" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_311850170" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/311850170" />
    <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions"><img alt="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464118116p2/2602702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/311850170?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions">Christina (A Reader of Fictions)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=yabc-reviews">yabc-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=series-not-finishing">series-not-finishing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer311850170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18207349573824410785">My review style is, and always will be, to write up my review right after I complete the book, and I do mean right after. If I can't write the review, I will save the last chapter until I have time. Doing otherwise would allow me to slack off, and I would never get anything reviewed, as well as giving me time to forget the book. The downside of this reviewing method, one I just have to accept, is that occasionally I have to try to compose a meaningful, coherent review while shell-shocked by what</span>
  <span id="freeText18207349573824410785" style="display:none">My review style is, and always will be, to write up my review right after I complete the book, and I do mean right after. If I can't write the review, I will save the last chapter until I have time. Doing otherwise would allow me to slack off, and I would never get anything reviewed, as well as giving me time to forget the book. The downside of this reviewing method, one I just have to accept, is that occasionally I have to try to compose a meaningful, coherent review while shell-shocked by what I've just read. Bear with me, as The Madman's Daughter definitely left me feeling a bit dazed.<br /><br />On a lot of levels, I'm really not entirely sure just how I felt about this novel. One thing that I do know quite for sure is that Shepherd writes well. Her syntax and diction dovetail with the historical setting, and never once threw me out of the book. Though much of the novel consists more of suspense than outright action, Shepherd kept the story tense and me on the edge of my couch.<br /><br />Littered throughout The Madman's Daughter are literary references. Of course, the novel itself retells H.G. Wells' The Island of Dr. Moreau, which I have not read. However, my perusal of the Wikipedia article convinces me that Shepherd reworked the story with a deft hand. In addition to this, she sprinkled in numerous references to Shakespeare, including The Tempest, a very apt work to be brought up in this instance. There is even a reference to X-Men, though not, obviously, so overt of one, since it didn't exist back then.<br /><br />What I found myself utterly unprepared for was how utterly dark, gruesome, creepy and horrifying this book is. Had I read Wells' work, I would have been better informed of the coming experience, but I knew nothing. Yes, the cover hints at creepiness, but this turned out to be one of the scariest books I have ever read. Of course, suspense has always been my weak point, as well as some other issues that I'll tackle next. Shepherd hits most of the staple varieties of horror: not knowing who to trust, fearing darkness with in oneself, mad science, gore, suspense, chases and more. Were I a big reader of horror, I do not know that I would have marked this as a must-read, but, let me tell you guys, you want this.<br /><br />However, I know a lot of people, myself included, have a big issue with animal death in novels. For me, kill a human and I'm rarely bothered; kill a furry, adorable creature and I will ugly cry. An animal dies in an awful way in chapter two, and over the last half of the novel focuses on just vicious, awful things done to animals in the name of science. Again, were I familiar with Dr. Moreau, I would have known, but... If you're seriously concerned, my recommendation would be to read Wells' novel or a summary of it online, because I suspect Shepherd's is darker than the original, based on my sole Wells experience.<br /><br />Juliet Moreau has a lot of sass and she made a delightful main character. I rooted for her along the way, which only made the horror that much more terrifying. Juliet's father, the infamous Dr. Moreau died, and, eventually, her mother did as well, leaving her to the charity of family. Unfortunately, her extended family turns out not to be at all charitable. Pulling on an old connection of her father's, she manages to obtain work at King's College as a maid, sunk low in prospects and station. At the college, Juliet is sexually harassed in the first chapter. I worried about whether she would have enough spunk to be an interesting main character, but, believe me, this girl holds her own once she is not trying to keep her job anymore.<br /><br />Shepherd also excelled at Dr. Moreau, who fits the mad scientist role to a T. Not really a spoiler because obviously: he's actually alive. He also very much comes across as a man of the time period. So many historical novels depict most of the characters as rather modern with regards to women's rights, particularly those appealing to female readers. Dr. Moreau has no such conceptions, believing women are to be married to the men their fathers say, and that they should do nothing but needlework and piano playing until that time comes. Juliet, feisty and clever, struggles against how he wishes her to behave.<br /><br />Sadly, I was not so fond of her love interests, Montgomery and Edward. Yup, a love triangle strikes again, though not one of the most annoying ones. I will credit Shepherd with not making it insanely obvious which man would be her choice, and with making both of them very obviously flawed, though neither one ranked as swoon-worthy for me. The love triangle reminded me somewhat of that in Griffin's Masque of the Red Death, though I felt a bit more sure in The Madman's Daughter which guy would win in the end. However, the ending did surprise me, so bonus points for that.<br /><br />Do not let the lovely cover fool you: The Madman's Daughter is horror through and through. Though not for the faint of heart, Shepherd has constructed a well-written and clever retelling, sure to delight fans of creepy tales.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18207349573824410785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_484499088" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/484499088" />
    <a title="Kat (Why Read)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6167480-kat-why-read"><img alt="Kat (Why Read)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561313835p2/6167480.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/484499088?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat (Why Read)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat (Why Read)" href="/user/show/6167480-kat-why-read">Kat (Why Read)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6167480-kat-why-read?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer484499088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11307732393209614775">"To me blood smelled like home..."<br/><br/>I have a love/hate relationship with anything goth-emo-horror. I love to read it, but hate to be scared or creeped out. Terrify me and I resent you. But do nothing and I shall call you "bunny". See you can't win.<br/><br/>I remember The Island of Dr. Moreau movie when I was little. My older brothers were obsessed with it and kept it on repeat in the VCR. While I was usually around when it was playing, I can only remember snippets from covering my eyes. When I heard this w</span>
  <span id="freeText11307732393209614775" style="display:none">"To me blood smelled like home..."<br /><br />I have a love/hate relationship with anything goth-emo-horror. I love to read it, but hate to be scared or creeped out. Terrify me and I resent you. But do nothing and I shall call you "bunny". See you can't win.<br /><br />I remember The Island of Dr. Moreau movie when I was little. My older brothers were obsessed with it and kept it on repeat in the VCR. While I was usually around when it was playing, I can only remember snippets from covering my eyes. When I heard this was inspired by that, I knew the meat of the story but the potatoes were still foggy. So reading about the relationships of the characters in this novel was new and unmarred. Yet I doubted there was much that could get to me at my age.<br /><br />So with much doubt, I embarked on reading this novel (at my own risk). It gave me waking nightmares! I can't get the twitching rabbit out of my head.....GAH! Even when I said bunny earlier I thought of the one in the book and it made my flesh crawl. Ewww. And yet I read this front to back with my morbid curiosity driving me. I couldn't stop turning the pages no matter how gross or eerie things got. The ending was more a relief... I felt as if I had escaped the island of Dr. Moneau. Nonetheless, this was an exciting journey.<br /><br />The dynamics of the characters was complex. There was no definite evil person or saint. At times Juliet was as fragile as a lamb and others where she was as fired up as a wildcat. Dr. Moreau was no cookie cutter villain either. There was much to each character then first observations.<br /><br />There were enough elements sure to captivate the adoration of every reader:<br />♥ romance<br />♥ suspense<br />♥ action<br />♥ mystery<br />♥ religion cults<br />♥ murder<br />♥ monsters<br /><br />This was also way more mature than your average YA book. You will find yourself forgetting that the character is only sixteen.<br /><br />This was definitely retro with an edge of creepy! The cover fooled me. It looks like one of those historical fictions with language that will put you to sleep long before the story line catches. But rest assured, the gore picks up right away. The narrator's solemn situation and peculiar circumstances keeps you turning. There romance was only dished in hints, then it was right back to crazyville. Insane &amp; magnificent in it's freakiness!<br /><br />Even in my dreams I can't escape the mental imagery of this novel which is why I have no choice but to rate it "EPIC"! <br /><br />GOTHIC THRILLER, INDEED!<br /><br />I could wax poetic on the many things I loved about this but I'll leave the rest for you to discover on your own.<br /><br />I look forward to future novels this author has to offer. <br /><br />*I received an ARC from the publisher for review and honest feedback.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11307732393209614775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1109329708" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9573067368589643111">Possibly this isn't a very original idea, but anyway.<br/><br/>Ladies and gentlemen, I present to you the high school yearbook version of <i>The Madman's Daughter</i>!<br/><br/><b>Moreau Island High School</b><br/><br/><i>School slogan: No is not a word</i><br/><br/><b>The Students:</b><br/><br/>Juliet Moreau<br/><br/>Has the potential to become best student of the year...if she gets out of her own way.<br/>Brains and beauty in one package...not that the boys noticed her brains.<br/>Naturally talented at everything...so naturally daddy issues.<br/><br/>Hobbies: Dissecting, angsting, daydreaming<br/><br/>Favouri</span>
  <span id="freeText9573067368589643111" style="display:none">Possibly this isn't a very original idea, but anyway.<br /><br />Ladies and gentlemen, I present to you the high school yearbook version of <i>The Madman's Daughter</i>!<br /><br /><b>Moreau Island High School</b><br /><br /><i>School slogan: No is not a word</i><br /><br /><b>The Students:</b><br /><br />Juliet Moreau<br /><br />Has the potential to become best student of the year...if she gets out of her own way.<br />Brains and beauty in one package...not that the boys noticed her brains.<br />Naturally talented at everything...so naturally daddy issues.<br /><br />Hobbies: Dissecting, angsting, daydreaming<br /><br />Favourite song: Haunted by Taylor Swift<br /><br />Voted "Most Indecisive Personality of the Year"<br /><br />Quote: "I’d thought I was so clever. I thought I could see past his manipulations. But I’d heard only what I wanted to."<br /><br /><i>Editor's comment: When Juliet was born, I'm pretty sure deus ex machina sat up, took notice and said, "Hallelujah! Finally I got someone to play with!"</i><br /><br />Montgomery...I don't know his name<br /> <br />The school jock with an obvious heart of gold...and less obvious brains of iron. 'Cause they're obviously rusty.<br />Popular with the girls...of all species.<br />Good at everything and anything...except doing what common sense demands.<br /><br />Hobbies: Body-building(?), secretly experimenting, home economics<br /><br />Favourite song: You Belong With Me by Taylor Swift<br /><br />Voted "Most Likely to Succumb to Parental Expectations"<br /><br />Quote: ""It's not this island keeping us from being friends."<br /><br /><i>Editor's comment: The good doctor made a mistake. It was Montgomery that was born without a spine, not Juliet.</i><br /><br />Edward Prince<br /><br />The dark horse that nobody wants to approach...because he is creepily like another Edward from YA.<br />Survives a brutal 10-12 days at navy camp with no food or water...but can't resist the doe eyes of a teenage girl.<br />Intelligent enough to be successful...so yet again hampered by a dark past.<br /><br />Hobbies: Reading, staring intensely, haute couture<br /><br />Favourite song: Teardrops on My Guitar<br /><br />Voted "Most Likely to Found in a Dark Corner of the School"<br /><br />Quote: “Don’t run."<br /><br /><i>Editor's comment: Poor Edward. He had so much potential to be interesting. Unfortunately his cranium is programmed to give Juliet most of its space.</i><br /><br />Alice<br /><br />Barely worth mentioning here...but is here anyway.<br />Has a sweet disposition and appearance...so is the equivalent of a doormat.<br />Doesn't intend to cause any trouble...and does only that by making certain parties jealous.<br /><br />Hobbies: Gardening, Montgomery, sewing<br /><br />Favourite song: Love Story<br /><br />Voted "Least Likely to Be Remembered without an Yearbook"<br /><br /><i>Editor's comment: Not really sure which Shakespearean play has an Alice in it. Is it the one by Lewis Carroll?</i><br /><br />The Teachers:<br /><br />Principal Moreau<br /><br />Possibly the most sadistic, inhumane academic who ever lived, Dr.Moreau founded Island High School as a testing ground for ground-breaking, heart-breaking new 'educational' theories. He can often be found in the chemistry lab, trying to get the formula for a perfect student just right. Don't let the bloodstains on his coat put you off; he's quite approachable and is willing to talk about anything so long as it centres around an operating table.<br /><br />Words of wisdom: "Don’t be alarmed if you’re awoken. The animals - they scream, you know. An unfortunate effect of vivisection."<br /><br />Mr.Balthazar<br /><br />The friendly, easy-going gym teacher. He may look positively grotesque, but beneath that is a sweetheart who just wants to be loved. The least paid among the teachers since the costs for breaking tennis racquets have to be taken out of his pay.<br /><br />Mr.Ajax<br /><br />You'll never see this Biology teacher coming. Literally. Well known for his propensity to sneak up on students texting in class. Strict but fair - he guts the students who don't do their homework, takes the others on a fieldtrip.<br /><br />Mr.Caesar <br /><br />You can hardly see this Theology teacher around, but he does turn up for classes. Rumour has it that he likes boating and is a fan of Rudolph the Reindeer. <br /><br />And that's it, folks! I've run out of steam. Not particularly impressive this time round, but I tried. You can't fault me for that, can you? On the other hand, so did the book, and look where that got it...</span>

<div id="review_476672423" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/476672423" />
    <a title="Scarlet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3839903-scarlet"><img alt="Scarlet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556098025p2/3839903.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/476672423?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scarlet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scarlet" href="/user/show/3839903-scarlet">Scarlet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=impressive-debuts">impressive-debuts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=disturbia">disturbia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer476672423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4077847345289685758"><b>3.5</b><br/><br/><br/><b>---Immediate Reaction---</b><br/><br/>I haven't read <i>The Island of Dr. Moreau</i> so I had no idea what to expect going in, but this was surprisingly good - in a dark, twisted way. The last few chapters were a thrill ride. I wouldn't have guessed the plot twists in a million years.<br/><br/>I have my reasons for the somewhat low rating (more on that later) but for now, I just wanted to say this: <b><i>The Madman's Daughter</i> is a very strong debut in the horror genre</b>.<br/><br/><br/><b>---Full Review---</b><br/><br/>An intriguing start and an amazing end, marr</span>
  <span id="freeText4077847345289685758" style="display:none"><b>3.5</b><br /><br /><br /><b>---Immediate Reaction---</b><br /><br />I haven't read <i>The Island of Dr. Moreau</i> so I had no idea what to expect going in, but this was surprisingly good - in a dark, twisted way. The last few chapters were a thrill ride. I wouldn't have guessed the plot twists in a million years.<br /><br />I have my reasons for the somewhat low rating (more on that later) but for now, I just wanted to say this: <b><i>The Madman's Daughter</i> is a very strong debut in the horror genre</b>.<br /><br /><br /><b>---Full Review---</b><br /><br />An intriguing start and an amazing end, marred by a somewhat listless middle part – that is how I sum up <i>The Madman’s Daughter</i>.<br /><br />The book starts off on a very promising note. We are introduced to Juliet Moreau, an orphan from a once-prestigious London family that fell victim to a horrible scandal. She ekes out a living working as a maid in a med school. I found Juliet a very fascinating character – sensible, resolute, toughened by circumstance, with occasional hints of something inexplicably dark shining through. It was gripping and sinister, exactly how I expect a horror novel to be.<br /><br />And then, it just fizzled out.<br /><br />I have two theories for why that happened.<br /><br />1. <u>The Love Triangle</u>.<br /><br />I’m not a fan of triangles in general, but I don’t mind one if it’s necessary to the plot and done well (like in <i>The Hunger Games</i>). Except the triangle here is neither. Even on the island, where there are such deliciously creepy things to focus on, Shepherd spends a lot of time building Juliet’s love dilemma. And it’s frustrating. One minute, Juliet’s worrying about the strangeness of the island, and then suddenly, she’s wondering how so-and-so’s hands would feel on her skin or how so-and-so’s lips would feel on her <i>pulsing veins</i>. Meh.<br /><br />2. <u>The Blurb</u>.<br /><br />Maybe this doesn’t apply to people who have already read <i>The Island of Dr. Moreau</i>, but I felt the blurb gave away too much information. Like what Dr. Moreau was actually doing/creating on the island. It’s difficult to remain interested when you already know crucial things that the protagonist is yet to figure out.<br /> <br />Somewhere around Chapter 30 though, things got good. And I mean, <b>really, really good</b>. The pace shot up drastically, the suspense was excruciating, and the revelations made me shudder. <i>The Madman’s Daughter</i> assumed all the eeriness of a cult horror classic.<br /><br />Megan Shepherd is a fine writer. Her prose captured the sinister atmosphere of the island really well. I noticed something interesting about her use of similes though:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> Fear spread throughout my body like an infection.<br /><br />My head throbbed as if my skullcap was fitted too tight.<br /><br />Something about it lodged a dull pain in my side, as if a fractured rib now pierced my right lung.<br /><br />A chill tiptoed up my spine, one vertebra at a time.<br /><br />His lips grazed my neck, and my larynx tensed, ready to scream.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />See what she did there?? Quirky. I like that ;)<br /><br />Overall, <b><i>The Madman’s Daughter</i> was quite an enjoyable read that could have been better had the focus remained on the horror elements of the story and not the romance.</b><br /><br />A well-earned 3.5 stars.<br /><br /><u>P.s.</u> Fellow animal-lovers beware. Parts of this book can make you extremely queasy.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4077847345289685758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1416195183" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1416195183" />
    <a title="Jessica ❥Chatterbooks Book Blog❥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37057510-jessica-chatterbooks-book-blog"><img alt="Jessica ❥Chatterbooks Book Blog❥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471840369p2/37057510.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1416195183?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❥Chatterbooks Book Blog❥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❥Chatterbooks Book Blog❥" href="/user/show/37057510-jessica-chatterbooks-book-blog">Jessica ❥Chatterbooks Book Blog❥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15720399-the-madman-s-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37057510-jessica-chatterbooks-book-blog?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37057510-jessica-chatterbooks-book-blog?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1416195183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8655694538497761747">Dark, strange, mysterious, intriguing, and twisted are all words that I would use to describe this book. It was the perfect October read! I absolutely love the atmosphere of this book. The setting added so much to the feeling of the overall story. I don't think if it was set in present day and another place that it would have the same effect. The book had an ominous feeling throughout and you could just feel that things weren't going to end well. There were no happy endings in this story. <br/><br/>The ch</span>
  <span id="freeText8655694538497761747" style="display:none">Dark, strange, mysterious, intriguing, and twisted are all words that I would use to describe this book. It was the perfect October read! I absolutely love the atmosphere of this book. The setting added so much to the feeling of the overall story. I don't think if it was set in present day and another place that it would have the same effect. The book had an ominous feeling throughout and you could just feel that things weren't going to end well. There were no happy endings in this story. <br /><br />The characters were very interesting. There was Juliet's father, Dr. Moreau, a deranged, cold, and completely unhinged man of science; Montgomery, the Moreau family's ex-servant, Juliet's best childhood friend and love interest, as well as Dr. Moreau's assistant in all things; Edward, a handsome castaway with a mysterious past and strong affection for Juliet; and the creepy deformed islanders with different levels of intelligence and morals. I enjoyed reading this story through the main character, Juliet's perspective. I loved that she acknowledged the little bit of darkness inside of her, the part that reminded her that she was indeed her fathers daughter. Despite that, Juliet was not a bad person by any means. She was inquisitive, smart, and compassionate. She was not however, a dainty, innocent, young girl. She was determined, brave, and she stood up for herself even when others may have ran or given in. Juliet had seen and experienced enough in her life to know the darker side of man. She was very wishy washy when it came to her love interests, but I wasnt bothered by that too much. <br /><br />The plot was well paced and kept me interested for the duration of the story. I did not see the twist at the end coming which was refreshing because I usually do. The ending made me want to immediately go out and buy the next book. I can't wait to see what else is store for Juliet in the next installment in this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8655694538497761747" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1RJgx79N9tW3j3XsJt8mCBDPBylnXZxtTY23BRBdXOUhotq5236H8H3QUdNyaWCehvLljzJ3U+Csf8V6Yztr1A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TqtOHGrkeHFBj2nvYOQXF8SJLLzKJbKHN8jfzetV8ca6G/RiDtcJVIvQTdA0UlGBUrTOGp8PfQrWOq2ymDPG9w==')})
  }

She is the author of several young adult and middle grade novels. She now lives and writes on a 125-year-old farm outside Asheville, North Carolina, with her husband, two cats, and an especially scruffy dog.</span>

            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_16182308').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
